class="article-header"><div class="article-meta article-meta-upper"><div class="eyebrow"><a href="/category/us/us-regions/midwest/wisconsin">Wisconsin</a></div><div class="article-date"><strong>Published</strong><time> 1 hour ago</time></div><!----></div><h1 class="headline">Wisconsins Supreme Court strikes down governor's safer at home order</h1><!----><!----><div class="article-meta article-meta-lower"><div class="author-byline"><!----><span>
        By
        <span><a href="/person/p/morgan-phillips">Morgan Phillips</a><!----><span class="article-source"><a target="_blank" href="http://www.foxnews.com/"> | Fox News</a></span></span></span><!----></div><div class="article-social"><div class="social-icons"><ul><li class="fb"><a href="#" rel="nofollow">Facebook</a></li><li class="tw"><a href="#" rel="nofollow">Email</a></li></ul></div></div></div></header><div class="article-content-wrap sticky-columns"><div class="article-content"><div class="article-body"><div class="featured featured-video video-ct" data-v-275a95fe=""><div class="contain" data-v-275a95fe=""><div class="control" data-v-275a95fe=""><a href="#" class="top" data-v-275a95fe=""></a><a href="#" class="close" data-v-275a95fe="">close</a></div><div class="video-container" data-v-275a95fe=""><div data-widget-type="embed" data-video-id="6025576909001" data-video-domain="foxnews" class="m video-player" data-v-275a95fe="" data-embed-uid="fnc-embed-1"><div class="video-container"><iframe aria-label="MVPD Picker" src="//static.foxnews.com/static/orion/html/video/iframe/vod.html?v=20200511164417#uid=fnc-embed-1" border="0" allow="autoplay" scrolling="no" style="width: 100%; height: 1px; min-height: 100%;" mozallowfullscreen="" webkitallowfullscreen="" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0"></iframe></div></div></div><div class="info" data-v-275a95fe=""><div class="caption" data-v-275a95fe=""><h4 class="title" data-v-275a95fe=""><a href="http://video.foxnews.com/v/6025576909001" data-v-275a95fe="">Fox News Flash top headlines for May 13</a></h4><p data-v-275a95fe="">Fox News Flash top headlines are here. Check out what's clicking on Foxnews.com.</p></div></div></div></div><p class="speakable"><strong>Get all the latest news on coronavirus and more delivered daily to your inbox.&nbsp;<a href="https://www.foxnews.com/newsletters/coronavirus" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">Sign up here</a>.&nbsp;</strong></p><div class="ad-container mobile"><div data-iu="ban1" class="ad gam"></div></div><div class="ad-container tablet"><div data-iu="lb2" class="ad gam"></div></div><div class="ad-container desktop"><div data-iu="lb2" class="ad gam" id="desktop_desk-art-pol-lb2" data-ad-size="728x90,300x250,320x50,300x50,1x1,fluid" data-ad-lz="1" data-ad-init="1" data-google-query-id="CM7Mx_-SsukCFVJqwQodfoUBTA" data-ad-slot-rendered="1" data-rendered-size="1x1"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/4145/fnc/desk/art/pol/lb2_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/4145/fnc/desk/art/pol/lb2_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/4145/fnc/desk/art/pol/lb2_0" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" style="border: 0px none; vertical-align: bottom; width: 1px !important; height: 1px !important;" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="4" data-load-complete="true" width="1" height="1" frameborder="0"></iframe></div></div></div><p class="speakable"><a href="https://www.foxnews.com/category/us/us-regions/midwest/wisconsin" target="_blank">Wisconsins</a>&nbsp;Supreme Court struck down the state's&nbsp;safer at home order Wednesday, saying Democratic Gov. Tony Evers administration overstepped its authority when it extended the order through the end of May.</p><p>The court ruled four to three in a case brought forth by Republican lawmakers that sought to block the order issued last month by Evers top health secretary, Andrea Palm.</p><p><a href="https://www.foxnews.com/us/illinois-country-decides-to-reopen" target="_blank"><strong>ILLINOIS COUNTY DEFIES GOVERNOR, VOWS IT'S 'BACK OPEN FOR BUSINESS' DURING CORONAVIRUS OUTBREAK</strong></a></p><div class="ad-container mobile"><div data-iu="ban2" class="ad gam"></div></div><p>All future lockdown orders must go through the legislature, the ruling said. The Safer at Home order will remain in place for six days, giving the legislature time to come up with new guidance in coordination with Evers' office, according to the court.</p><div class="ad-container tablet"><div data-iu="lb3" class="ad gam"></div></div><div originalimageurl="https://cf-images.us-east-1.prod.boltdns.net/v1/static/694940094001/61384252-5eca-4581-b4b7-c5a73770ff89/7693c70c-3419-436f-93e1-89316eb7ba76/1280x720/match/image.jpg" class="embed-media fn-video"><div class="video-container"><div data-widget-type="embed" data-video-id="6156461678001" data-video-domain="foxnews" class="m video-player" style="width:100%;height:100%;"><a href="http://video.foxnews.com/v/6156461678001"><img src="https://cf-images.us-east-1.prod.boltdns.net/v1/static/694940094001/61384252-5eca-4581-b4b7-c5a73770ff89/7693c70c-3419-436f-93e1-89316eb7ba76/1280x720/match/image.jpg" alt="Growing concerns about coronavirus effects following spike in rare condition afflicting children"><span class="overlay">Video</span></a></div></div></div><p>Evers issued a stay-at-home order in March which was supposed to expire April 24. But the Department of Health and Human Services Secretary Andrea Palm, an Evers appointee, extended it to May 26.</p><p>Republicans asked the Supreme Court on April 21 to block the extension, arguing that it amounts to an administrative rule, which requires legislative approval.</p><div class="ad-container mobile"><div data-iu="ban3" class="ad gam"></div></div><p>Evers administration argued that state law clearly gives the executive branch broad authority to enact emergency measures to control communicable diseases. Attorney General Josh Kaul also noted that Evers' order was similar to that in at least 42 other states and has saved many lives.</p><div class="ad-container desktop"><div data-iu="lb3" class="ad gam" id="desktop_desk-art-pol-lb3" data-ad-size="728x90,300x250,320x50,300x50,1x1,fluid" data-ad-lz="1" data-ad-init="1" data-google-query-id="CPiYyoWTsukCFdF_wQodTq0B8A" data-ad-slot-rendered="1" data-rendered-size="1x1"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/4145/fnc/desk/art/pol/lb3_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/4145/fnc/desk/art/pol/lb3_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/4145/fnc/desk/art/pol/lb3_0" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" style="border: 0px none; vertical-align: bottom;" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="5" data-load-complete="true" width="320" height="50" frameborder="0"></iframe></div></div></div><p>Chief Justice Patience Roggensack wrote for the majority that the order equates to an emergency rule that Palm can't enact unilaterally. The order creates criminal penalties that Palm has no authority to create, she added.</p><div class="ad-container tablet"><div data-iu="lb4" class="ad gam"></div></div><p>Rule-making exists precisely to ensure that kind of controlling, subjective judgement asserted by one unelected official, Palm, is not imposed in Wisconsin, Roggensack wrote for the majority.</p><div class="ad-container mobile"><div data-iu="ban4" class="ad gam"></div></div><p>During oral arguments last week, Justice Rebecca Bradley suggested Palms decision to extend the order without legislative input amounts to tyranny, according to <a href="https://wkow.com/2020/05/13/breaking-safer-at-home-order-struck-down-by-state-supreme-court/?utm_medium=social&amp;utm_source=twitter_WKOW" target="_blank">WKOW</a>.</p><p><strong><a href="https://www.foxnews.com/category/health/infectious-disease/coronavirus" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">CLICK HERE FOR FULL CORONAVIRUS COVERAGE</a>&nbsp;</strong></p><p>"I think there is a problem with the legislature giving away this much power to an un-elected cabinet secretary," said Bradley. "The people never consented to a single individual having that kind of power."</p><div class="ad-container mobile"><div data-iu="ban5" class="ad gam"></div></div><div class="ad-container tablet"><div data-iu="lb5" class="ad gam"></div></div><p>Rebecca Dallet, a liberal dissenting Supreme Court justice, wrote that the court's decision will undoubtedly go down as one of the most blatant examples of judicial activism in this court's history. And it will be Wisconsinites who pay the price."</p><p><strong><a href="https://www.foxnews.com/apps-products?pid=AppArticleLink" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">CLICK HERE TO GET THE FOX NEWS APP</a>&nbsp;</strong></p><div class="ad-container desktop"><div data-iu="lb4" class="ad gam" id="desktop_desk-art-pol-lb4" data-ad-size="728x90,300x250,320x50,300x50,1x1,fluid" data-ad-lz="1"><img src="//global.fncstatic.com/static/v/all/img/clear.gif" data-src="//global.fncstatic.com/static/v/all/img/clear.gif" alt="placeholder" class="ad-uvl-3" style="width:1px; height: 1px;" data-lz-init="1" data-lz-done="0"></div></div><p>The high court also backed Republicans over the liberal governor in holding in-person voting in April for the presidential primary amid coronavirus.</p><div class="ad-container mobile"><div data-iu="ban6" class="ad gam"></div></div><p>Wisconsin has faced&nbsp;10,902 cases of coronavirus and 421 deaths. Deaths have been in the single digits for 9 of the last 14 days.</p><div class="ad-container tablet"><div data-iu="lb6" class="ad gam"></div></div><p><em>The Associated Press contributed to this report.&nbsp;</em></p><!----></div><div class="article-meta"><!----></div><footer class="article-footer"><!----><!----><div data-uid="ar-2" class="vendor-unit tablet-desktop"
